y="583"></use></g></g></g></g></g></svg></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-3">\begin{align*}

P_{X^*} &= XC((XC)'(XC))^{-1}(XC)'\\
&= XC[C'X'XC]^{-1}(XC)' \\
&= XC[C'X'XC]^{-1}(XC)'\\
&= XC[C^{-1}X^{-1}X'^{-1}C'^{-1}]C'X' \\
&= XCC^{-1}X^{-1}X'^{-1}C'^{-1}C'X'\\
&= XCC^{-1}(X^{-1}X'^{-1})C'^{-1}C'X' \\
&= XCC^{-1}(X'X)^{-1}C'^{-1}C'X' \\
&= X(X'X)^{-1}X'

\\
\blacksquare
\end{align*}</script></div></div><p><span>Note that </span><span class="MathJax_SVG" tabindex="-1" style="font-size: 100%; display: inline-block;"><svg xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" \hat{y} &= X\hat{\beta}_{OLS} \\

note, we can see also that the residuals </span><span class="MathJax_SVG" tabindex="-1" style="font-size: 100%; display: inline-block;"><svg xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" width="1.082ex" type="math/tex">e</script><span> do not change as y on X* and y on X maintain the same dependent variable, such that.</span></p><p><span>These results imply the invariance of fitted values and residuals to nonsingular transformations of the independent variables.</span></p><p>&nbsp;</p><hr /><p>&nbsp;</p><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong><span>(b) As an application of these results, suppose that every X was multiplied by a constant, say, a change in the units of measurement. Would the fitted values or residuals change when we rerun the regression?</span></strong></p><p>&nbsp;</p><p><span>Multiplying the independent variable by a constant (diagonal matrix) indicates a nonsingular transformation of the independent variables. We have shown in (a) that these transformations have no effect on the fitted values/residuals.</span></p><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong><span>(c) Suppose that X contains two regressors </span><span A_{11}^{-1}+A_{11}^{-1}A_{12}FA_{21}A_{11}^{-1} & -A_{11}^{-1}A_{12}F\\
-FA_{21}A_{11}^{-1} & F
\end{bmatrix}</script></div></div><p><span>Where </span><span class="MathJax_SVG" tabindex="-1" style="font-size: 100%; display: inline-block;"><svg xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" X_{1}'X_{1} & X_{1}'X_{2}\\

\end{bmatrix}


\begin{bmatrix}
\hat{\beta_{1,OLS}}\\
\hat{\beta_{2,OLS}}
\end{bmatrix} = 

\begin{bmatrix}
X_{1}'y\\
X_{2}'y
\end{bmatrix}</script></div></div><hr /><blockquote><p><strong><span>Digression on Matrix Properties:</span></strong></p><p><span>To solve a system of equations using the inverse of a matrix A, note the following property:</span></p></blockquote><div contenteditable="false" spellcheck="false" class="mathjax-block md-end-block md-math-block md-rawblock" id="mathjax-n84" cid="n84" mdtype="math_block">

x="907" y="-213"></use><use xlink:href="#E85-MJMAIN-AF" x="422" y="246"></use></g><g transform="translate(4348,0)"><use xlink:href="#E85-MJMATHI-58" x="0" y="0"></use><use transform="scale(0.707)" F &= (X_2'X_2-X_2'X_1(X_1'X_1)^{-1}X_1'X_2)^{-1} \\
 &= (X_2'X_2-X_2'P_XX_2)^{-1} \\
 &= (X_2'(X_2-P_XX_2))^{-1}\\
 &= (X_2'(I-P_X)X_2)^{-1} \\
 &= (X_2'\bar{P_X}X_2)^{-1}
\end{align*}</script></div></div><p><span>Similiarly, solving for </span><span class="MathJax_SVG" tabindex="-1" style="font-size: 100%; display: inline-block;"><svg \hat{\beta}_{2,OLS} &= (X_2'\bar{P_X}X_2)^{-1}X_{2}'y-(X_2'\bar{P_X}X_2)X_2'X_2(X_1'X_1)^{-1}X_{1}'y \\

&= (X_2'\bar{P}_XX_2)^{-1} +X_2'\bar{P}_Xy
\end{align*}</script></div></div><p><em><span>By factoring</span></em></p><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong><span>(b) Alternatively, write (7.9) as a system of two equations in two unknowns </span><span (X_1'X')^{-1}(X_{1}'X_{1}\hat{\beta}{_{1,OLS}}+X_{1}'X_{2}\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}} &= X_1'y )\\
\hat{\beta}{_{1,OLS}}+(X_1'X')^{-1}X_{1}'X_{2}\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}} &= (X_1'X')^{-1}X_1'y \\
\hat{\beta}{_{1,OLS}} &= (X_1'X')^{-1}X_1'y -(X_1'X')^{-1}X_{1}'X_{2}\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}}\\

X_{2}'X_{1}((X_1'X')^{-1}X_1'y -(X_1'X')^{-1}X_{1}'X_{2}\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}}) +X_{2}'X_{2}\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}} &= X_2'y \\


X_{2}'X_{1}(X_1'X')^{-1}X_1'y-X_{2}'X_{1}(X_1'X')^{-1}X_{1}'X_{2}\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}}+ X_{2}'X_{2}\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}} &= X_2'y \\


X_{2}'X_{1}(X_1'X')^{-1}X_1'y -X_2'{P}_{X_1}X_2\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}}+X_{2}'X_{2}\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}} &= X_2'y \\

X_{2}'X_{2}\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}}- X_2'{P}_{X_1}X_2\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}} &= X_2'y -X_{2}'X_{1}(X_1'X')^{-1}X_1'y\\


(X_{2}'X_{2}-X_2'{P}_{X_1}X_2)\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}}&=X_2'y -X_{2}'X_{1}(X_1'X')^{-1}X_1'y\\


(X_2'(X_{2}-{P}_{X_1}X_2))\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}}&=X_2'y -X_{2}'X_{1}(X_1'X')^{-1}X_1'y\\


\hat{\beta}{_{2,OLS}} &= (X_2'\bar{P}_{X_1}X_2)^{-1}X_2'\bar{P}_{X_1}y
\end{align*}</script></div></div><p><strong><span>(c) Consider regression with constant </span></strong></p><p>&nbsp;</p><p>&nbsp;</p><p>&nbsp;</p><p>&nbsp;</p><p>&nbsp;</p></div>
